text:
I used to make cinnamon rolls and stick buns professionally.  Here is how we rolled tight buns.  Make sure you roll your dough out to 1/4".  Apply butter evenly, then sugar/cinnamon mixture.  Holding the rolling pin, gently roll over the sugar/cinnamon mixture.  At the beginning of the roll only 1/2" of dough and pinch down.  Now you must begin rolling from each corner, middle, working your way back and forth.  Curve your corners toward the center to avoid too much overlap (exess)  IMPT:  after about 2-3 rolls, carefully lift up each portion and pull away from you, this will "tuck" in the dough, be careful not to tear the dough.

A lot to remember, but after you get the hang of it, it's like second nature and you will have picture perfect cinnamon rolls and sticky buns

text:
This is a good cinnamon roll recipe.  Here's a trick for cutting the rolls without mashing the dough:  take a piece of thread, slide it under the roll, cross the thread and pull quickly.  It works like magic, and you don't have a sticky knife to clean up afterwards!

text:
Mine weren't so ooey-gooey.  I made per the recipe---except I didn't add the pecans to the brown sugar/cinnamon mixture that went inside the rolls.  I would suggest not melting the butter that you spread on the inside before you roll it up.  If you just spread on a thin layer of softened butter you should end up with a more ooey-gooey feel because you'll have more butter on the inside to melt, which will make the caramel more gooey.  When you use the melted butter you don't get a lot of butter on the inside & I found this tended to give me a dryer--but still good--caramel roll.  I will try again, but next time I won't melt my butter.
Have made a couple more times & it definitely works better not to melt the butter for the inside and then I double the caramel for the bottom.  Still a good recipe, hence the 4 stars, but does need some adjustments.

text:
The best!!  I come from a long line of bakers.. this is great!  I used half whole wheat flour...incredible.  To easily cut the dough, use dental floss.  Slide it under the end, cross the dental floss at the top and pull.  Perfect cuts every time!  If you want more ooey-gooey, just add a little cream or whole milk (3-4 tablespoons) to the butter, brown sugar mixture in the pan.

text:
Great Recipe! For those of you who are novice bakers like myself, I'll share a few things I learned after a lot of trial and error and more reading. First, this recipe should be read closely as there are a lot of steps and can be confusing. Kneading was the difficult part for me. You must knead at least the recommended time if doing it by hand (8min for this recipe). In the past I didn't knead enough and my bread didn't come out fluffy, I couldn't figure out what went wrong because the dough would rise nicely. Kneading is key!! Add a little flour if it gets too sticky to work with/ lightly dust. The dough should feel harder the more you knead and you'll know its ready when you pinch it between your fingers and it feels like your earlobe. If in doubt, knead some more. It is difficult to over knead by hand. Also, when making the caramel you may want to do extra. I made double but make sure the sugar has completely dissolved so that it turns into caramel. I think it should be cooked at medium-high heat but watch carefully so it doesn't burn. Lastly, I cooked at 375 for 25min (min time recommended) and I was disappointed that after all the work they were over cooked on the top. I don't know if the temp was too high or time was too long, just make a note and watch carefully. No one mentioned this in other reviews so maybe it was just my oven. Next time I will try 350 degrees...My first review on here so hope it was helpful :) Good Luck!!

We loved this breakfast treat! It IS time consuming (I had to start these by 8am so that they'd be done for our brunch at around 11am) but they were very good! We only had to bake for 18-20 minutes (as another reviewer stated) and they didn't "dry out" for us. I noticed other complaints that they tasted stale when cooled...but we didn't have that problem since we don't like cooled caramel rolls anyways. The few that were leftover were reheated a few hours later this afternoon in the microwave for a few seconds and tasted as good as the original batch out of the oven! I'll be sure not to lose this recipe! Thanks Jen!

text:
This is a fabulous recipe. No major changes are necessary and it's super easy to make. Definitely a holiday stale from here on out. 
Here are a few notes I wanted to share:
Pressed for time in the morning?  Make the dough the night before and refrigerate overnight in an oiled and covered bowl. It will rise slowly throughout the night. Just make sure you pull out the dough a few hours before you make these so it has time to get to room temperature. 
The step for spreading the melted butter and cinn sugar on the rolled out dough: I used room temp butter instead of pouring a liquid butter on the dough.  Much easier (spread w a spatula). 
We went loco with the cinnamon, using much more then it called for. You can't go wrong with too much cinn (we ended up using about 1/4 and it was soooo fantastic). I would reccomended it!
If you can get two people (4hands) to roll it up you will get a great roll. Make sure to roll out the dough evenly. I didn't and though they were still great there were some rolls that were smaller from the ends and the middle ones were fit for a king!
Don't be afraid to increase the butter and sugar and nuts that go on the bottom f the pan. The more "ooey-gooeyness" the better!
Just some helpful tips. Enjoy!

text:
This is my second time making these.  (I often use the Ninety Minute Cinnamon Rolls on this site, because I never seem to plan far enough ahead.)  That being said, I really planned ahead this time and made the rolls the night before, placing the pan in the fridge overnight still covered with the damp cloth from the first rise.  Perfect!  Take them out about 35 minutes before you plan to bake and let them come to room temperature.  Bake as directed.  Gooey and delicious and the long, slow rise makes them very light.

These are delicious.  They are time-consuming, but easy to prepare.  The crumb of the dough is right on.  However, I have one CAUTION: If you do use a 9X13 inch pan, make sure it is at least a couple of inches deep.  Otherwise, all that delicious buttery caramel will be burned to the bottom of your oven, creating awesome amounts of blue smoke and a gross cleaning situation.

This was fabulous!  VERY good.  I've even made the dough over night, stored in the fridge, and finished up in the morning, to kind of cut down on time.  The only suggestion I would make would be brush the dough with melted butter before putting in the oven, and again about 10 minutes into it.  This keeps it moist, and prevents the "hard dough" thing from happening.  I do make this once a week for Sunday breakfasts before church- and have made for bake sales.

None
text:
I have been using this recipe for four years. At first the results were disappointing but after some trial and error, I came to the following conclusions:

1.) Roll those buns tight! Practice makes perfect. Consult youtube to get a sense of proper rolling technique.

2.) Double the caramel, and add a pinch of salt, a splash of milk and some sort of liqueur. I've even used Malibu and the results were insanely delicious. The sugar melts effortlessly-- no graininess.

3.) Allow plenty of time for the first and second rise, especially the second. The fluffier they are right before they bake, the better. Use a brownie pan so the buns are packed tightly together and have space to rise UPWARD, not outward.

4.) Tent your pan with foil so the buns cook evenly and don't brown too much on top. Every oven is different so be careful with temperature and cooking time-- took me several batches to figure my own oven out.

Happy baking, AllRecipes community :)

text:
I LOVE cinnamon buns and have tried numerous recipes, in an attempt, to duplicate the buns my grandmother made when I was a chid. She was a fantastic cook/baker but, unfortunately, did not leave recipes for several of her wonderful treats. I must admit these delicious buns are very close. I followed the recipe exactly as printed except I only required 3 1/2 cups of flour, total, to achieved a perfectly silky smooth elastic dough. I also added 1 tsp vanilla and let the buns rise about 2 hrs initially  and 1 1/2 hrs the second rise. This produced a wonderfully flaky bun which is delicious with or without the caramel pecan topping. My husband and grandchildren said these are the best I have baked thus far. I encourage anyone considering cinnamon buns to try this recipe....you will not regret it.

With a few changes, this is a fabulous recipe.  As another reviewer noted, 15 buns didn't fit well into a 9 x 13 pan; when I realized this, I had to made more sauce for the second (8x8) pan.  The total amount of sauce I made (which I thought was just the right amount to make them nice and gooey) was 1 1/c cups butter and 1 1/2 cups brown sugar - this was enough sauce to generously cover the bottom of both pans. I read several comments about them being over cooked so I baked them at 350 for 20 minutes - perfect!  Thanks for sharing this great recipe.

text:
I am not sure how you could not love these!  They are the best sticky buns I have ever had...hands down! One tip I found that shortened the overall prep time was "proofing" the buns in the oven. You just have to heat your oven to 200 degrees F and then shut it off. Any time you need them to rise (in the bowl and in the pan) you can just cover them with the damp towel and place them on the middle rack of the warmed up oven. I noticed that some people said it was time consuming so I did this to speed it all up. It really did the trick. I also only had to bake them for 20 minutes. Over all it only took 1 hr and 45 minutes to finish them as the dough only had to rise for 30 minutes the first time around and then the buns only had to rise for 20 minutes before baking.

text:
Great recipe but hard to get out of the pan after baking because the praline hardened and stuck - even with a parchment lined pan.  Next time I will IMMEDIATELY invert onto a serving plate after baking. For the filling I mix SOFTENED butter with the cinnamon etc and use an off-set spatula to spread that mixture on the dough instead of brushing MELTED butter then sprinkling the cinnamon etc on.  I find this yields a gooey-er and softer bun. :)  I use dental floss to cut the individual buns - way easier than using a knife.

text:
I was disappointed with the recipe. I cut the dough in half, making one 9-inch round pan of sticky buns, and one of cinnamon rolls. The bake time is woefully too long, resulting in a burned sugar mess on the bottom of the sticky bun pan.  

I will try again, making the following changes:
Use a bread machine to make the dough.
Add a bit of nutmeg to the dough.
Spread softened butter over dough & then sprinkle with cinnamon & brown sugar for the filling.
Use thread or dental floss to cut the rolls.
Add 2-4 T. cream or milk to the "ooey gooey" topping in the bottom of the pan. (And I may just cube cold butter & sprinkle in the bottom of the pan with the brown sugar rather than melting together.)
Change from metal to glass pans in an effort to prevent burning.
Bake at 350 degrees for 18 minutes -- and start checking at 15 minutes.

city:

country:
None
text:
These were excellent!  I took it for granted that the hubby (who requested cinnamon buns, and therefore became the baker's apprentice today) would know that a stick of butter is 1/2 c.--he didn't.  So, I learned after these went into the oven that he had only used 1/2c. butter instead of 3/4 c. for the bottom of the pan.  It didn't matter in the end.  Changes I made:  I don't like to use saucepans when a microwave will do.  So, I microwaved the butter when it called for a saucepan.  To make the brown sugar and butter meld together in the microwave, I first microwaved the butter until melted, then added the brown sugar, stirred, then microwaved an additional thirty seconds.  I have a high-wattage microwave, and 30 sec was fine for this.  I let the dough ball rise overnight, then let it rise for an additional four hours after forming it into the buns.  My house is quite cold, so I let them rise in the microwave, which carries a residual heat.  We doubled the filling.  We used whole pecans.  Delicious, quick, and easy!  Will be using this one again.

text:
This is an excellent sticky bun or gooey cinnamon bun recipe.  I made the dough exactly as written.  These are the changes I made to the filling and topping:  I used 1/2 cup raisins soaked in rum (to plump them) in the filling.  The topping I increased to 1 cup each, butter and brown sugar and added 3 Tbsp's pancake syrup to it (you could use honey, maple syrup or corn syrup).  I think it made the topping more typical of a sticky bun, which was what I wanted.  It wasn't grainy and didn't harden at all.  It thickend to a nice sticky caramel sauce upon cooling.  I used the full cup of chopped, toasted pecans for the topping.   Husband absolutely raved about them.  Will definately make these again.  Thanks, Dakota Kelly, for the great recipe!

text:
The bread recipe for these is wonderful.  However, I followed the recipe exactly, and there is not nearly enough filling or goo in the bottom of the pan for these to be called "ooey-gooey".  In fact, they didn't have any "goo drip" at all, and the filling was barely enough to cover the rolled out dough.  The flavor is great, but they are more of a pecan sweet roll than a cinnamon bun/roll.  They reheat in the microwave to be just as good as they were the night before from the oven.  The next time I make these, I'll just double or triple the filling and double the goo in the bottom of the pan; that will make them 5-star.

text:
First of all, I started by warming up the milk first so it could cool while I dissolved the yeast and sugar.  Then when both were ready, I put the milk mixture, the yeast mixture, the eggs and the flour into my kitchen aid mixer with the mixing piece on low speed to combine them. I also used the same setting to mix in each 1/2 c. addition of flour until the last one. When there was only 1/2 c. of flour left, I changed from the mixing piece to the dough hook to complete the mixing of the flour and then I turned the speed up and let the dough hook and my kitchen aid to do the kneading for me.  Then I did the rest as directed.  
Doing it this way took out alot of the manual labor and I had more time to do other things.
These rolls were very sweet and perfect! Try the recipe as written first then make changes the next time if needed.  You may be suprised with the initial results!

https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/80519.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Totally a hit! Used 3.5 cups flour in my mixer and found the dough was too dry, so I used a little more milk to make it a little stickier.  Then used the other 1/2 cup to flour the surface and knead it to the right texture. Doubled the cinnamon brown sugar mixture for the bottom of the pan. Added the pecans. Spread soft butter on the rolled out dough. Added another 1 Tbsp of cinnamon to the brown sugar and cinnamon mixture for the inside. Added pecans. Let it rise in a warm oven for the first and second rise. Baked it in a glass 13x9 glass dish at 375 degrees for 18 mins. Buttered the tops of the cinnamon buns. Turned them over on a dish and all the ooey gooey topping stayed on top of the buns. The dough was soft and the topping was fabulous.  Did not use the icing as it would have been too sweet. This is my go to recipe for cinnamon buns as long as I live!

Well worth the effort. Excellent recipe as is. I do tinker with recipes, however, so I went for the ooiest gooiest I could get. Used a tad more yeast, because this dough is resilient and I wanted height. Added a tad more brown sugar and butter to the pan bottom (must distribute right into the corners) A few more pecans... A tad more brown sugar and cinnamon onto the dough. And then cut the roll into 14 pieces, rather than 15. They were tall, tender and gooey. Friends came by unexpectedly and now they think I do this sort of thing everyday. As for stale leftovers? What leftovers!

text:
These were very good!  I've been searching for the perfect pecan roll for years and this is definitely the closest I've come.  The dough part of this recipe is pretty much the exact same recipe as the Clone of a Cinnabon recipe on this site...just a tad more of this or that, but ultimately the same.  I think next time I may use the Cinnabon dough recipe (I like what is different about that recipe-a tad sweeter) with this caramel topping. I only made 6 rolls (froze the other half of the dough for later), but I didn't halve the caramel topping.  While it was de-lish that way, I think next time I'll only 1 1/2 the recipe, just to be a *tad* more healthy (can you even use that word here?).  I also followed the advice of reviewers who said to take them out early, and I won't do it again, they were completely doughy still.  I cooked them about what the recipe states.  They did get quite brown on top though.  Once they start getting brown, I'll cover them with a piece of foil next time for the rest of the cook time.

text:
I did this recipe minus the ooey-gooey (personal preference). The dough was a little dry when mixing it, so I took the suggestion of other reviews to add a little splash of milk. I also used instant yeast instead of active dry, as that was all I had on hand. I used 0.20 oz (20% less) of instant yeast instead of the 0.25oz of active dry yeast, and then I just followed the recipe (including proofing, or dissolving the yeast in the water and sugar). I lengthened the rising time for around half an hour on the first rise just because I had the patience and time to do so =P. For the sugar-cinnamon filling, I added an extra 1/2 TB of cinnamon for extra cinnamony yumminess, and I also used softened butter instead of melted. I cut the dough using the dental floss method, as recommended by others (take a piece of dental floss and wrap it around the log, and make a knot and pull). This resulted in perfectly round rolls! I also cut the baking time in half, because mine were already done within 10 - 12 min. The buns turned out perfect! The dough was very soft, a little moist, and delicious. Yay!

text:
Ooey, gooey, and oh-so chewy! These came out great!
 I didn't have any pecans, so I substuted walnuts and after reading some of the other reviews, I only put them in the bottom of the baking dish and it worked out great!
 Also, as another reviewer suggested, I didn't melt the butter which was spread on the inside of the rolls, I only let it become very soft and easily spreadable, and that worked out great too.
 To make sure these come out their very best make sure the butter/brown sugar mixture is thoroughly heated through before pouring it into the bottom of your baking dish. Enjoy!

text:
I followed the recipe for the actual rolls themselves to a tee with the following exception: I used 3t active dry yeast (I'm always paranoid that my bread won't rise properly!). I completely omitted the "goo" at the bottom of the pan because organic butter (or even conventional butter for that matter) is so expensive. Lastly, I used the icing recipe from Clone of a Cinnabon for the icing just because I had already tried it and really liked it. I baked them at about 335 for about 18 minutes just to get a more even "doneness" and to make sure they didn't get too brown. Next time I will also take the advice of another reviewer and start the milk mixture before the yeast mixture as it saves a few minutes of waiting. The dough rose well for me (both rises). Next time, I will allow about 2.5 hours for the second rise to get a fluffier, lighter roll. My rolls could have stood some more rise time. I baked mine on a cookie sheet (separated) and then iced them immediately. I had been using the Clone recipe, but wasn't ever able to get the dough to rise hardly at all (I think because of the lack of instructions for those with no bread machine). This one worked out perfectly for me. Thanks for sharing this one! Kudos to you, Jen!

This recipe is pretty good. I made it with rapid rise yeast, which cut down on the wait time. I did not do the gooey in the bottom of the pan. Instead i amped up the cinnamon to 1 1/2 tsp in the filling and added 1 c semisweet mini chocolate chips also to teh filling. I baked them in 2 9 inch glass pie plates for 19 minutes and served them warm as dessert. My guests were weeping with joy and begged to take some home. With the rapid rise be sure to follow instructions on the packet. My rise times were 10 minute for first rise and 30 for final rise.

These buns are incredible. My Grandma always made what we called "Sticky Rolls" every Thanksgiving and Christmas.  You had to snatch them quickly because they didn't last. These buns are in the same ballpark as those buns, but Grandma's were still better; her cinnamon/brown sugar/butter mixture solidified in places, which lent a candy like texture to the buns. But you can't go wrong with this recipe. Everyone will like them. The tip for cleanly cutting the buns with dental floss was spot on. It works like a charm. My late grandma--bless her soul--would get a big laugh if she knew I was bragging about her buns!

text:
Super yummy.  Here are my modifications (thanks to other reviewers!):
1.  Lined pan with parchment - parchment was oversized so I flipped up the edges for the last 8 mins so none of the caramel would overflow. Also it made it easy to flip over into the same  pan - less clean up!

2.  Made them overnight so after the second proof, covered with plastic film and then with a dish towel and stuck it into the fridge. Brought back to room temperature.

3.  Instead of melting the butter, just softened it for 20 seconds in the microwave.  

4. Gave them an eggwash before putting them in the oven.

5.  Baked at 350¬∞F for 20 mins and the turned up the heat to 375¬∞F for the last 8 mins. Cooked through perfectly without over cooking the top (or is that the bottom?).

text:
This was my 1st attempt at making Cinnamon rolls from scratch. I am very glad that I tried it. Do yourself a huge favor and use the video. If I had tried to use just the recipe, I would have not been successful.

These are wonderful. I made a few mods to fit my taste. For example, if you like Cinnamon,  you will probably be a bit disappointed with the recipe as is. I added about a 1/4 cup of Cinnamon to the topping. The recipe calls none. I love Cinnamon so you will have to adjust based on how much you like. I also added some Ginger and Cloves for an extra kick.

I also added 8 ounces of Cream Cheese to the topping because, I thought as is, it sounded bland. I am very glad I added all this, because they turned out great. For me, the sweetness came out just right, so this will also depend how much sweetness you like.

I have made a few changes, as my mom is a cook and thus was able to help: 
- For the milk, I used half and half. 
- If making a double recipe: 3 tbsp. ground cinnamon for the filling. For the glaze: 2 cups brown sugar and 2 cups butter. 
-Lower the oven temperature to 350 degrees. Bake until golden brown (start at 25 minutes and check).

I've made it several times, each time improving. Will continue to make as they are delicious when done correctly.

text:
The absolute best! I don't know which came first, but this is exactly the same recipe  as in the Canadian Living's Bread and Pizza book.

I make my dough in a bread machine. If you want to do this, add the dry ingredients to the baking pan first, followed by the milk and eggs. My bread maker has a separate compartment for yeast and dispenses automatically. If yours does not have a yeast compartment, just add the yeast last.
Prep the filling while the bread maker does it's thing.

The bread maker mixes everything and does the first rise.
Then follow the recipe from "Punch down the dough...".

Works perfectly every time!

I am a novice when it comes to working with yeast and this was only the 4th or 5th I've tried.  Followed this recipe to the letter except I sprinkled a little extra cinnamon on top at the end (only had a few sprinkles left to use up in the jar and figured it couldn't hurt...it didn't)

Awesome recipe and will definitely be trying again and again!

text:
I was really hopeful of this recipe based on reviews. They turned out good just not great. I love to cinnamon rolls to have flavor all around each layer in the bun itself. The only parts that had the most flavor were the inside parts. I think I can make it perfect next time though. It also needs a glaze which is also really easy to make. Here is what I'd do differently. 1. I'd put the brown sugar mix on top of the the whole dough from edge to edge that way I'm not wasting any dough. 2. I'd double the mixture that goes on the bottom of the pan and put that second mix on top of the cinamon rolls when theirs 5mins of baking left. 3. I'd make a glaze. That way you get flavor through and through. I will say that the good thing about these rolls were that they were pretty buttery and moist. But then again that might've been due only to me laying a layer of butter on top the last 10mins of baking because I was afraid of having a crunchy and dry top. I also took these out at 15-20mins. They were stil cooked all the way through.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
My family loved these.  We ate two each right off the bat, but my tummy wished I'd only had one, what with all the dough and sweetness.  This recipe was fairly simple and fun too, but a long haul, what with having to rise the dough for a total of two hours.  If you need cinnamon rolls, and you need them now (!), then a recipe without yeast will satisfy sooner.  But if you want the real, ooey-gooey thing, then take the time with the dough as required.  I had left over melted butter in the end as using two whole tablespoons on the outside of the roll prior to baking was not needed, nor stuck to the roll.  I agree with MNDiana, who suggests brushing on softened butter, rather than melted butter, and will try that next time.  I used walnuts and raisins instead of pecans, and found the 375 temp a little too high as my outside rolls got a little too brown and crusty in just 22 minutes, but the inside rolls were perfect.  Lastly, the filling on the bottom of the pan cools to a candy-like state quickly and is hard to remove from pan onto the top of rolls after baking without it being clumpy, so make sure to tip them out onto another dish (after loosening the edges with a butter knife) after just a minute after removing from oven, and leave the tray upside down for a couple more minutes to let the filling fall onto the buns.  This will coat the buns evenly and prevent it from hardening onto the bottom of the pan before you can scrape it all off onto the buns! Merry Munching!

The only thing that wasn't exactly as expected was the gooey topping -instead of a gooey sugary topping, it became a caramel topping (that even hardens like a Halloween candy anywhere that pooling has occurred, though a quick microwave loosens it up again). 

The dominant caramel flavor was not what I was expecting, though from several other comments mentioning it this seems to be what others sought, so I assume I did follow the directions correctly (I went over them thinking I must have done something wrong, but it seems that I did everything exactly as expected).

The rolls were simple perfection. I will just try to adapt this for a non-caramel topping next time.

I've tried this recipe twice now. I think the results would be a bit more consistent with a weight-based recipe and not a volumetric recipe (especially relevant to us in countries where metric measurements are used) - and after making the necessary conversions, it was much better the second time around. AWESOME!!! Adding my own touches to this recipe. I used my mixer stand with the dough attachment to elimate kneading the dough for 6 to 7 minutes. I also doubled the caramel. I did not melt my butter, I used soften butter, spread it on the rolled out dough before the brown sugar, cinnamon & pecan mixture. Rolled the mixture with the rolling pin to stay put on the dough. Then used thread to make precise cuts. Best served Warm. Husband LOVES it warm and gooey.

I just made for the second time and they came out better. The first time i made it exactly like the recipe is written, the second time i tweaked a bit. I add more of the sauce that goes under the cinnamon buns, and i also add a bit of salt, vanilla to the sauce. The salt makes a big difference, it makes the flavors pop. I also add more cinnamon and sugar to the filling. What really helped them come out moist is that i let them rise for a longer time and I put them to rise in a warm oven. I would turn on the oven for a minute and then turn it off real quick. I did have a thermometer inside the oven to monitor the heat because the yeast dies at 140 degrees, I never let it get past 125 degrees.This is definetly one I will be making over and over again. Love them.

text:
I have tried a number of cinnamon roll recipes and this is the best of the bunch!

Rather than pour the sugar/butter/pecan mix directly on the bottom of the pan I first placed parchment paper on the pan and then added the mixture. When I inverted the pan and pulled off the paper almost every bit of the sticky goodness was on the top of the rolls and the pan was spotless.

This recipe creates a wonderful soft, moist, but not doughy middle. Not sure how some managed to get dry rolls out of this! Maybe over-baking?

The only real problem I had was that I used a full sized cookie sheet, not the smaller pan dimensions suggested, and the buns fit just perfectly packed in right next to each other, but the sheet overflowed into the oven and instead of a nice, yummy cinnamon bun scent in the air, I got a burning smell and smoke :/ Probably I need to get a big baking pan. Amazing :) My only critic is that these belong in a bigger pan than 9x13!! It is way too small and the rolls end up squished. I stole a few suggestions from others, such as: to cut the rolls without mashing the dough take a piece of thread, slide it under the roll, cross the thread and pull quickly. For the sauce I used 1 1/4 cup of butter with 1 1/4 cup of brown sugar instead of the 3/4s of each that is suggested. And I did not melt the butter that you spread on the inside of the dough, I just used extremely soft butter and rubbed that onto the dough with my hands which made the filling alot more ooey gooey. :) But still an amazing recipe.

text:
Great recipe... :) inside of rolling these into traditional cinnamon rolls, i made "cinnamon holes".. The middle is always the best part isn't it? Well the way i made them each bite was like eating the middle piece.   Instead of filling the dough after rolling it out, i cut little squares out and put 6 pieces into the bottom of a muffin tin, then layered on some of the filling, a few chopped pecans, then layered again 7 more dough squares and poured some more filling on top with more pecans and then let rise as usual and baking time differed just a little,.. i kept an eye on them so they wouldn't over cook.. BUT YUMM-O! and not much more effort to make these even better than they already were. :)

These sounded tempting & since I have a son who loves cinnamon rolls, I thought I would give this recipe a shot. After reading many of the reviews, I thought I needed to make a little extra caramel sauce for the bottom so I increase the butter and sugar just a tad.  The sweetness was overpowering.  We couldn't enjoy the rolls because of the rich topping.  I guess if you're not looking for an incredibly rich topping, don't increase the ingredients.I was under the impression it wouldn't be enough coating.  I am sure we would have enjoyed it more, if I had stuck with the original recipe.  Too much of a good thing is distracts from the roll itself.  If I brave the process again, I will make it according the recipe.

text:
If I could give this recipe 6 stars, I would. I topped my [12 large] cinnamon buns with cream cheese icing after they had cooled down a bit, and I'm not gonna lie, these are some of the best cinnamon buns I've ever had. Everything about this recipe is great, but you have to be prepared to put in the time, about 3.5 hrs to frank. 

This was my my first time making cinnamon buns, or any yeast pastry, and this wasn't too difficult (though I have baked before). Before the first proof I thought I had messed up my dough because it was really rubbery and hard to knead, but after it sat for an hour it was much softer. I had trouble rolling it out too because, like puff pastry, it wouldn't stop shrinking back to a ball. Eventually I got it rolled out (18x14" is smaller than you think) I filled it with [about] 3/4 cup brown sugar, 1/4 cup (not fresh) ground cinnamon, and 1/2 a cup butter. This made for a rich, thick cinnamon swirl guaranteeing a moist pastry. I only made 12 buns because you NEVER want to crowd them, they will grow when they proof AND when they bake. The large sweet sticky cinnamon buns this left me with makes this is my new go to recipe.

I don‚Äôt normally write reviews but I thought this one was worth it.  I wanted to make mini cinnamon rolls so after rolling out the dough into the 18x14 inch rectangle I then cut the rectangle into two pieces each 18x7 inches.  I filled and rolled each rectangle so each filled roll was 18 inches long.  I then cut with dental floss (highly recommend) resulting in rolls that were approximately 1 inch high (more or less).  Based on other reviews I also doubled the topping.  I was a bit worried when I put the rolls in the pan with the topping ‚Äì they looked like they were swimming in it.  I brought these to a potluck where I baked them there so they probably rose for 3 hours for round 2 of rising.  They really grew and they were no longer drowning in topping when served.  It was the perfect amount.  The cinnamon rolls were devoured and I received many compliments for them.  Definitely worth making  :)

text:
This is a really good recipe and it does take long, I was really satisfied with the result, but I did make some changes:

1. I made more of the butter/brown sugar mixture to pur in the pans
2.I used round cake pans instead of square
3.I didn't have a lot of pecans so I crushed some walnuts too
4.the dough was too dry - i made 1/2 cup of a milk/water mixture to add to the dough for it to get to the right consistency, when I added too much, I just added a bit more flour, I kept doing this until it was right
5.For whatever reason, my dough was refusing to rise, I popped them in the oven any way and they still came out great
6.Keep the oven lower, I baked mine at 330 Celsius
7. I used a lot of butter on the dough before adding the sugar/cinnamon mixture
8.I used much more than 3/4 cup of brown sugar when I was applying it to the dough: I made sure it was completely caked in brown sugar/cinnamon and nuts before rolling 
 
finally here is a critical caveat: I used round cake pans that are not perfectly sealed at the bottom, I had to place a rectangular pan on the rack below the buns so that it could catch the leaking sugar/butter.  When I did this, it burnt my rectangular pan and set off my fire alarm - don't worry! Because it had absolutely no impact on the cinnamon buns themselves, it just got ridiculously smokey in the oven/apartment. Or, just use a pan that is sealed at the bottom (I know, obvious)


if you are reheating them, dash a tablespoon of water on each one before putti

text:
Everything was going well (I followed the recipe to the 'letter') I only say that because I'm always accused (by my family) that I NEVER follow a recipe.  That's only because people create recipes and some steps just don't make logical sense (anyway, off on my soap-box).  However.  I followed all the steps from the video recipe and it was great...until I got to the part where I put the batch back in the oven to bake for the final product.  Disclaimer: the end pieces I placed in the oven to bake during the last rise of the buns, so I kinda guessed that it wouldn't take the allotted time that the recipe said to bake it for.  So, I shaved 10 minutes off.  Even with removing 10 minutes from the low end of the time allotted, they baked faster and when I took them out of the oven...they were not ooey gooey, but a little hard and sweet (except for the ones in the middle)  

Anyway.  I will bake them again because I will not let a recipe defeat me (smile).  My suggestion to anyone reading this, is to 1) While the buns are going through their last rise (after they've been placed in the sticky mixture) bake the ends that you trim off, just to get a gauge how long they may bake in your oven 2) After you've started baking, check the rolls after they have been in the oven for half of the time you're allotting to bake them.  Just to ensure that they don't get hard.  As that was very disappointing and I would hate for that to happen to anyone else.

Lastly, the flavor was great and this is

text:
Delicious! Bye- bye recipe I've been using for 20 years! I made these as 2" rounds once baked for a large brunch (I find people eat more when they are small).  I rolled the rectangle to 8" w, used only 1/3 of the butter, brown sugar and pecans indicated for the bottoms, made a mash of them and "buttered" the bottoms of the buns  before baking, spacing them like cookies so they did not touch while baking. Once putting them in the pan, I patted them down so that the "mash" was evened out underneath before letting them rise the second time. Baked them for 10 min on parchment, let them rest a couple min, put new piece of parchment on top of buns and then flipped them over onto new parchment. Scraped extra topping from old parchment onto  buns.

country:
None
text:
This is a great recipe and a big hit in my house! I followed the recipe to the T except I 
a. Added vanilla paste to the milk/butter mixture to impart some flavor into the dough itself. 
b. Added a little cream to the milk for more flavor.
c. Added honey to the butter before brushing it on the dough and sprinkling the cinnamon sugar on top. 
d. left the pecans out of the filling and only used it as a topping.

However (at no fault to the recipe creator) the video is very misleading.  Firstly, I've made this recipe quite a few times now & my dough never turns out like it does in the video. It is a really sticky dough before the first proof. Also, I'm convinced the lady in the video used different measurements for the brown sugar butter mixture. It WILL NOT come out anywhere near  that thick being that we're using equal parts . It is much more like a water. I do add more  sugar to make it thicker and avoid having a soggy top.

All in all, while this recipe is time intensive (any yeast leavened dough is) it really is so fun to make and customize the fillings to your taste. And in the end you will have something so delicious that everyone will rave about.

text:
I've made this recipe a few times and with a few tweaks I figured it out. I always use tinfoil or parchment paper for easy cleanup. I took another reviewer's suggestion to add pancake syrup (not maple syrup) to the topping (about 1/3 cup or so) and I HIGHLY recommend this. I also added 3 TBSP coffee cream from another reviewer suggestion and about half a cup more of each butter and brown sugar. The topping was gooey and perfect!!

My oven runs very hot and i think the recipe needs adjustment anyways for baking time, my first recipe I followed the directions exactly and it was very hard and dark and I could hardly eat them. So I adjusted the temperature by 25 degrees less and cooked covered with tinfoil for 20 min. Then 5 minutes without the tinfoil. I baked them in a 9x13 metal cake pan. They browned perfect and tasted amaaaaaazing! Best cinnamon buns I've ever made and I have been around the cinnamon bun block. 

A few more tricks I use: butter the inside with soft instead of melted butter, use toothfloss or string to cut the cinnamon buns (mint will not alter the flavor), roll them tight, and let them rise a  ton longer than the recipe says especially the second time. If you use tinfoil and it sticks to the pan, run hot water into it under your tap, let it soak a minute and it should peel off. Wrap your buns immediately in tinfoil to trap the heat and moisture until they are cool enough to eat. I dump mine straight onto tinfoil after the three minutes and cover it with more

I have a sticky bun recipe I have been making since high school that everyone loved.  I tried these and think I like them better. I made the dough in my kitchenaid stand mixer and was alarmed it seemed very wet/loose, so I added an extra 1/2 cup flour. As it turns out, I'd accidentally added double the butter. (One should not bake while packing school lunches/convincing children to brush teeth, etc.)  It worked out, thank God. The recipe made 16 huge rolls. 

I followed other reviewers' advice about doubling the butter /brown sugar and I regret it. Waaay too much caramel for my tastes! I feared I'd go into a sugar coma if I'd tried to eat a whole roll with its portion of caramel. 

Next time, I'll follow the original amounts. I'll also bake four and freeze the rest, unbaked, in packages of four each. That should be a year's worth of pecan sticky rolls for us.

text:
Amazing recipe!! I only added one additional step, after baking, I turned them over onto a cookie sheet and I noticed they didn't look as "sticky" as I had hoped for. I melted 1/2 cup brown sugar and 1/2 cup butter on low temp in a saucepan, heated on medium-low until bubbling and slightly thickened, poured over the top and sides of the buns. Added that extra stickiness and sweetness that took these to the next level. With this additional step, I rate these 5/5! I could eat the whole tray!

BEST GOOEY ROLLS I EVER HAD!!  I know if I made them every day every one of them would be eaten every day.... just toooooo good for words!  


I used my fav breadmaker recipe, then follow the directions for the filling and topping exactly.  The only thing I did different was I cooked the butter/b. sugar for the bottom of the pan, till dissolved.  Wow are these great!  

Made it the second time, and used Grandma's little trick to make them even gooey-er.  Before the rise in the pan, drizzle just a little bit of cream in the spaces between the rolls,  and the spaces around the edges.  They stay gooey-er longer, though in my house, the most they have lasted so far was over night!

Also make them with walnuts so yummy.

Can't even say how terrific this recipe is!

text:
Excellent recipe! 

I forgot to add the 1 tsp sugar to the yeast in the first step (didn't affect how it turned out). I used coffee cream instead of milk (the cream had to be used). I let the first rising go for an hour, and the second rising for for 1.5 hours. I set a timer for 25 minutes, uncovered, until 13 minutes were left, took them out and pressed them down a bit as they had "overinflated" somewhat. For the remaining 13 minutes I covered them in foil to prevent overbrowning of tops. After finished baking I took them out of pan immediately and covered them in foil on a plate until ready to be served. Super picky husband said this is the recipe I should keep- BIG statement for him to make.

Holy cow! This recipe must be foolproof, because I just made them never having made cinnamon rolls before AND without using measuring cups or spoons.

I made it because I'm visiting the family in Costa RIca that hosted me for my study abroad a couple years ago. They wanted me to make cinnamon rolls since they're somewhat exotic in Costa Rica, and THEY WERE SO GOOD. I definitely surprised myself. After eating two, my host mom was very impressed and said, "Ya puedes casarte." ("Now you can get married.")

Altitude note: We're at 6,000-7,000 feet here. I increased the temperature to 200 degrees Celsius and cooked them for about 32 minutes. When I took them out of the oven, they weren't quite brown on top but were definitely done enough.

I added a cream cheese frosting that was good: 2/3 cup cream cheese, 1 1/2 cups powdered sugar, 1 spoonful vanilla, 1/4 cup butter. (Measures are very approximate).

text:
We made this for Easter Brunch.  It is really an easy recipe, you just have to start it early to allow time for rising.  We started it early in the morning while we prepared other bruch food. We let it rise in the microwave - first put a medium bowl half full of water in microwave for about 3 -4 minutes, then when you take out the bowl of water rather quickly put the covered dough into the microwave and quickly close it and leave it undisturbed to rise.  When it's in the oven baking, next time I'll check it at about 22 -25 minutes, because 30 minutes made the bottom just a tiny bit too browed for me.  This is best served right from the oven, but it's delish no matter when you eat it!

text:
I was really looking forward to these, but they were too sweet and not moist enough.  I think the problem is the amount of brown sugar. This recipe calls for 1.5 cups brown sugar. Brown sugar should be measured packed, at 200g per cup, but in recipe that is way too much.  Too sweet, and it dries out buns. Indeed the topping was hard when it came out of the oven.  I would recommend using a total of 1 cup (200g) for the entire recipe. If you use a metal pan I also recommend 350 degrees instead of 375.

text:
i was so nervous trying this recipe out but boy was it worth it!! I followed the recipe almost exactly, with some minor changes as I could only find instant yeast that comes in 11gm packets where I live. I used about 1 3/4 teaspoons of instant yeast as the equivalent. I also let the dough rise for the same amount of time as above even with instant yeast. It's true what @JEWEL1190 notes that the longer you let them rise, the flufflier they become. And, instead of melting the butter, i brushed the butter at room temperature (I live in the tropical rainforest climate, everything melts at room temperature) over the dough and it worked out fine. The aroma in the house was incredible and by the time I served them, they were all gone in a matter of minutes. At everyone's request, will definitely do these again, even if it involves quite a bit of effort and bucket loads of patience. Well, you can alway reply emails, cook dinner or finish up a blog while waiting for the dough to rise. :) LOVE IT!

text:
I experimented a bit- I really like substituting butter with coconut oil so I was exited to try.  Everything went fine except the sauce & filling.(I split this recipe into 3 separate batches after the first proof (i.e. bread rising) 

My first batch with coconut oil instead of butter separated so had to dump it- the next caramel sauce and filling I did with butter and I used half a cup for both the filling and the topping sauce unfortunately I misunderstood the instructions and prepared my filling sauce the same way as the pan sauce-merely adding cinnamon-this resulted in a LOT of mess and most of the filling baked out:( so I used the rest of that as my topping sauce for the next batch. also the sauce on the first batch came out more like toffee than caramel :( started hardening even while still pretty hot. Also only needed to bake about 20 minutes-

The next batch I spread softened butter onto the roll & covered in the sugar mix. they rolled up nicely, & filling stayed in place but I had the same problem with the sauce and adjusted cooking time again.

The third I mixed the sugar mixture with a bit of softened coconut oil instead of melting it and used it like a paste for the topping which I spread over the tops and bottoms. for the filling I treated the coconut oil like the butter in the last one. the filling came out ok sauce not so much.
Bottom line- I would NOT cook with the sauce and instead make caramel sauce separately with the addition of milk. base dough = awesome

text:
Delicious! I made these cinnamon buns a total of three times, the second was a bit of a fail. You don't want to start making the cinnamon butter mixture until after you roll the dough out or it will get too hard. I like to bring it to a complete boil and then put it in the bottom of my pan. You also want to make sure you don't roll them too tight or they won't cook in the middle but will be hard on the outside. I also don't add all of the flour and Sift the cinnamon and sugar topping together:)

text:
the first time i tried this recipe, i followed it exactly and the caramel turned out more like candy - a bit hard, too sweet and baked for a bit too long.  the second time i added 1/3 cup low fat milk to the caramel mix on the bottom of the pan.  it stayed truly gooey and i liked it much better.  i also reduced the sugar by 2 Tbsp in the dough filling and didn't butter the dough before sprinkling the stuff on.  I reduced the baking time to 20 minutes and they came out perfect for me - light, fluffy, gooey and not too sweet.  thanks for sharing this awesome recipe!

text:
The buns themselves were great, although I think next time I would try just spreading butter into the rolls before adding the cinnamon and brown sugar, instead of melting it first. I found most of the sugar just went to the bottom of the pan with the suggested method.

Also, I would not bother with the butter/brown sugar mixture at the bottom of the pan. Mine did not turn out ooey or gooey at all. The mixture turned more into a fudge consistency, which tasted good at the bottom of the cinnamon bun, but I would rather just make a glaze or frosting to accompany the buns.

I would make this recipe again, but with a few very minor changes just to suit me a little better.

text:
This recipe is excellent! Takes a pretty long time to prepare, but is well worth it--better than any cinnamon buns you could buy. Some reviewers suggested doubling the filling, but I would highly recommend NOT doing that: I had a bit too much as it was! I also didn't use 4 cups of flour, but only 3-1/2 as that was all it needed. So, double the recipe 'cause they'll disappear fast!
